<span id="freeTextContainer10923647225374173911">'Growth can only truly be achieved through loss' (- A Mango Shaped-Space, by Wendy Mass) I love this quote because it demonstrates The pain and suffering that comes from loss but also the growth. In this book Mia discovers a huge loss that wounds her but also makes her 10x stronger. I feel like this was a great lesson for Wendy to put into her book. In a way i see it as 'when one door closes another door opens'. This is one of the many lessons I learned from this book. "Numbers don't have colors</span>
  <span id="freeText10923647225374173911" style="display:none">'Growth can only truly be achieved through loss' (- A Mango Shaped-Space, by Wendy Mass) I love this quote because it demonstrates The pain and suffering that comes from loss but also the growth. In this book Mia discovers a huge loss that wounds her but also makes her 10x stronger. I feel like this was a great lesson for Wendy to put into her book. In a way i see it as 'when one door closes another door opens'. This is one of the many lessons I learned from this book. "Numbers don't have colors, they simply have a shape and a numerical value, that's all" (- A Mango Shaped-Space, by Wendy Mass) This was a comment Mia's teacher at the age 8 said. It made me feel bad, And maybe even a little bit regretful because her teacher simply was being rude, And i can't even imagine the pain I would feel. But this comment helped Mia grow in so many ways she became an indented person and truthfully honest and I admire that. <br /><br />I would recommend this book to all people who love Really touching realistic books. I watched a fantasy girl grow up and become strong but at the same time i watched myself become a better human being and a better friend. This book has taught me so much and i am very happy i read it.</span>

<div id="review_1125599950" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1125599950" />
    <a title="Orinoco Womble (tidy bag and all)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20738920-orinoco-womble-tidy-bag-and-all"><img alt="Orinoco Womble (tidy bag and all)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406361683p2/20738920.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1125599950?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Orinoco Womble (tidy bag and all)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Orinoco Womble (tidy bag and all)" href="/user/show/20738920-orinoco-womble-tidy-bag-and-all">Orinoco Womble (tidy bag and all)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20738920-orinoco-womble-tidy-bag-and-all?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20738920-orinoco-womble-tidy-bag-and-all?shelf=rather-heavy-going">rather-heavy-going</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20738920-orinoco-womble-tidy-bag-and-all?shelf=d-is-for-dysfunctional">d-is-for-dysfunctional</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1125599950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4717406419324461426">A fast read for an adult, I pretty much finished it in a sitting. I wouldn't give it to any sensitive kids under about the age the main character is...eleven or twelve, because it could be upsetting. The book deals with a lot of loss and sorrow. (Are there any upbeat middleschool books out there anymore?) Before the action even starts you have one person who has lost her mother to disease and the MC's beloved grandfather has died too. And that's before you meet her odd family: her strangely supe</span>
  <span id="freeText4717406419324461426" style="display:none">A fast read for an adult, I pretty much finished it in a sitting. I wouldn't give it to any sensitive kids under about the age the main character is...eleven or twelve, because it could be upsetting. The book deals with a lot of loss and sorrow. (Are there any upbeat middleschool books out there anymore?) Before the action even starts you have one person who has lost her mother to disease and the MC's beloved grandfather has died too. And that's before you meet her odd family: her strangely superstitious younger brother who keeps records of all the Big Macs he ever ate on a wall chart with dates and times; her older sister who starts out as the "normal" one and suddenly morphs into a vegetarian neopagan (or whatever), and her oddly absent mother, who apparently is a SAHM and yet is blissfully unaware of what her kids get up to, and is emotionally cold. <br /><br />Secrets abound in this family, and when Mia's synasthesia surfaces, Mom's first reaction is denial ("you're making it up!"), the second is accusation (she turns to her husband and says, "This is all your fault!") and the third is treating it like a "disease"--rush off and get it "cured" because there's something "wrong" with Mia. (Yeah--and yet her strange little brother is "normal", right?) Dad works only a few days a week, but when the charputzka hits the family fan, he's always out of reach--up a ladder, up in his helicopter, or somewhere outside, away from it all. Even the family cat spends its time creeping around in crawlspaces and hiding from everyone. This is dysfunctional with a hey-nonny-no, and I found the ramshackle house that Gramps and Dad built at the same time (not "together," no one in this family seems to be able to collaborate on anything) but in totally different directions, with no evident blueprints (or indeed planning permits) to be a metaphor for this strange family.<br /><br />Did I like the book? Not a bunch. The title caught my eye because there are synasthesiasts in my own family and I have a mild form of it myself, though nowhere near as extreme as Mia's or the people she meets. (Sound has shape, if you want to know, but I don't see the shapes; rather, I percieve them as if they were inside my skin.) But the people and relationships were a bit more fraught than I care for. Crap, nobody's ever <i>happy</i> in that house. She can't even get along with her "best" friend. I had enough of that growing up, I don't care to read about it at such length. If you like dysfunctional families, you'll enjoy it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4717406419324461426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_240795306" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240795306" />
    <a title="Angie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7065153-angie"><img alt="Angie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/240795306?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie" href="/user/show/7065153-angie">Angie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240795306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11177206441618515394">So far, I think this is a very interesting book, because I have never seen anyone memorize things by colors. I never even knew what synesthesia was until I started reading this book. At certain times while reading this book, I wish I could experience a day with synesthesia, sensing colors like Mia Winchell. In addition, I enjoy reading the part when Mia is taking the math test. She struggles with memorizing the formulas by actual letters, then she uses her method of using colors during the test </span>
  <span id="freeText11177206441618515394" style="display:none">So far, I think this is a very interesting book, because I have never seen anyone memorize things by colors. I never even knew what synesthesia was until I started reading this book. At certain times while reading this book, I wish I could experience a day with synesthesia, sensing colors like Mia Winchell. In addition, I enjoy reading the part when Mia is taking the math test. She struggles with memorizing the formulas by actual letters, then she uses her method of using colors during the test and it turns out she gets a good score on it! <br /><br />Mia Winchell has synesthesia. She can hear sounds, smell colors, and see shapes. However, she keeps it as a secret from everyone. She uses colors to help her memorize everything. In addition, none of her family member relates and understands her very well. Mia feels alone that she is the only person that has it. As time passes by, she meets this boy who has the same situation as her in which she does not feel alone anymore. She is trying to find someone that can help her cure this problem because she wants know how it feels like to be a normal person.<br /><br />I absolutely enjoy reading this well-written and imaginative book and every time I read this, I it gets more and more interesting so I don't want to stop reading it! I am already half way through the book and I will try to finish it as soon as possible! </span>

<div id="review_92364790" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92364790" />
    <a title="Britt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3375474-britt"><img alt="Britt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1267915579p2/3375474.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92364790?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Britt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Britt" href="/user/show/3375474-britt">Britt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92364790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2081650544714316589">Britt van der Poel								 4-22-10<br/> A Mango-Shaped Space by Wendy Mass<br/><br/> A Mango-Shaped Space is about a girl named Mia who has synesthesia. The color for her name is a sunflower yellow, and the numbers get mixed up in math class all the time. Her parents freak out when she tells them, and when her cat dies all of her colors disappear. Mia is very confused about what to do in her life, but ends up finding a lot of friends who understand and respect her. Eventually, everyone in her class figures out</span>
  <span id="freeText2081650544714316589" style="display:none">Britt van der Poel								 4-22-10<br /> A Mango-Shaped Space by Wendy Mass<br /><br /> A Mango-Shaped Space is about a girl named Mia who has synesthesia. The color for her name is a sunflower yellow, and the numbers get mixed up in math class all the time. Her parents freak out when she tells them, and when her cat dies all of her colors disappear. Mia is very confused about what to do in her life, but ends up finding a lot of friends who understand and respect her. Eventually, everyone in her class figures out that she has synesthesia. They all start asking her what color their name is, and sooner or later, she becomes better in math. <br />	My favorite character was Mia because she was very independent and caring. She handled her situations by herself and didn’t give up. She was also very creative, and I liked her way of giving everyone a different color for his or her name. She didn’t care what other people said about her, and she always kept the people she cared about dearly in her mind. She seemed very much like me, so it was easy for me to connect myself to her. <br />	The climax of the story was when her cat, Mango, died. Mia’s colors disappeared and went straight to black and white for a couple days. She felt blanked out without seeing a bright, shiny color when looking at something. Mango reminded Mia of her Grandfather who died when she was seven years old. Whenever she looked at her cat, she would see his face and cry, thinking of the painting she threw away of him which she had painted herself. <br />	I think that the author wanted me to know that you should respect anyone no matter who they are. People can be nice no matter what they have or are. I think she also wanted the readers to know that you have to try in order to receive something. Mia really had to try to become better in Math, and she did. You just have to tell yourself to try a little bit harder. <br /> I would recommend this book to people of all ages. It is a suspenseful, interesting, and exciting book, and anyone who reads it will be impressed. <br />	I rate this book a 10 out of 10. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2081650544714316589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fGe1Lg/6ciZMpOSjt6KFZ2q3GgtfsUuEFVHSeT+BVjkAJJwyqWazN99HkKY45eVFL8mDz4on04pR1bINVczx2g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Vf2851hGKXkh2R8ZqaTUP88uLACDYvwZjLSjCtsia4spvpX7/troaLI6axwm47QdilC1xFb0ZBfIMMN+sW/MaA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17395524585241508863">Wendy Mass is the author of twenty-two novels for young people, including A Mango-Shaped Space, which was awarded the Schneider Family Book Award, Leap Day, the Twice Upon a Time fairy tale series, Jeremy Fink and the Meaning of Life, Heaven Looks a Lot Like the Mall, the Willow Falls, Space Taxi and Candymakers series. Wendy wrote the storyline for an episode of the television show Monk, entitled</span>
  <span id="freeText17395524585241508863" style="display:none">Wendy Mass is the author of twenty-two novels for young people, including A Mango-Shaped Space, which was awarded the Schneider Family Book Award, Leap Day, the Twice Upon a Time fairy tale series, Jeremy Fink and the Meaning of Life, Heaven Looks a Lot Like the Mall, the Willow Falls, Space Taxi and Candymakers series. Wendy wrote the storyline for an episode of the television show Monk, entitled "Mr. Monk Goes to the Theatre," which aired during the show's second season. She tells people her hobbies are hiking and photography, but really they're collecting candy bar wrappers and searching for buried treasure with her metal detector. Wendy lives with her family in New Jersey.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17395524585241508863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
